## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch reactor concentration ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a chemical species concentration A(t), which is the standard form of kinetic rate laws in homogeneous reaction kinetics. With only (t, A) available, the most likely models are empirical/mechanistic rate laws where the rate depends on A (reaction order, equilibrium relaxation, autocatalysis) and/or explicit time-dependence (time-varying conditions, deactivation, diffusion limits).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (rate independent of A; e.g., surface-limited with excess reactant)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay or pseudo-first-order conditions)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular with equal reactants or self-reaction)
- General n-th order law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order)
- Parallel pathways (mixed orders): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (two concurrent consumption channels)
- Source + first-order loss: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant generation with linear removal; CSTR-like or side-production)
- Relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (approach to steady/equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic / self-accelerating then self-limiting: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (rate peaks at intermediate A; autocatalysis with limiting capacity)
- Time-varying first-order coefficient (activation/deactivation): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (k(t) changes exponentially in time)
- Diffusion/fractal kinetics (time-dependent apparent rate): dA_dt = -c0 * t**c1 * A**c2 (power-law time dependence from transport limitations/aging)
- Induction period / delayed onset: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * t)) * A (rate ramps up from ~0 to steady first-order)
- Periodic forcing (e.g., light modulation): dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (consumption with oscillatory production/drive)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Straight-line test for order: if dA_dt is proportional to A**n, then log(|dA_dt|) vs log(A) is approximately linear with slope n (diagnoses power-law kinetics).
- Equilibrium approach signature: a linear dependence on (c1 - A) indicates exponential relaxation of A(t) toward a fixed point A = c1.
- Autocatalysis signature: a factor A*(c1 - A) implies zero rate at A=0 and A=c1 with a maximum at intermediate A (sigmoidal A(t) possible).
- Parallel pathways: sums of terms like (A, A**2, ...) indicate multiple independent reaction channels; dominance can switch with A.
- Induction/activation: multiplicative (1 - exp(-c*t)) indicates an initial lag where |dA_dt| starts near 0 and increases over time at fixed A.
- Deactivation/condition drift: multiplicative exp(c*t) or t**c on a base rate law indicates that the environment/catalyst effectiveness changes systematically with time.
- Source plus sink: an additive constant term in dA_dt implies net generation even when AŌēł0 (background formation, feed, or baseline production).
- External periodic drive: additive sin(c*t) (or similar) suggests forcing by cyclic inputs (illumination, stirring cycles), creating oscillations superimposed on kinetic decay.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
$$f(A) = -0.18997742423620262 \cdot A^2 + \frac{0.45987487478174419 \cdot A^2}{0.7497988950401423 \cdot A^4 + 1}$$

Note that this is a function of A only (no t dependence).

Let me simplify: Let me denote the GT as:
$$f(A) = -\alpha A^2 + \frac{\beta A^2}{\gamma A^4 + 1}$$

where ╬▒ Ōēł 0.19, ╬▓ Ōēł 0.46, ╬│ Ōēł 0.75.

This can be written with a common denominator:
$$f(A) = \frac{-\alpha A^2(\gamma A^4 + 1) + \beta A^2}{\gamma A^4 + 1} = \frac{-\alpha\gamma A^6 - \alpha A^2 + \beta A^2}{\gamma A^4 + 1} = \frac{-\alpha\gamma A^6 + (\beta - \alpha) A^2}{\gamma A^4 + 1}$$

This is a rational function of A. The key structure is $\frac{a_1 A^6 + a_2 A^2}{a_3 A^4 + 1}$.

For large A, this behaves like $A^2$ (from the $A^6/A^4$ term). For small A, it behaves like $(\beta - \alpha)A^2$.

**Key observation:** The GT is a rational function. Most candidates are polynomials (possibly with transcendental terms). A polynomial cannot exactly equal a rational function unless the rational function simplifies to a polynomial.

Let me check: does the GT simplify to a polynomial? No ŌĆö the denominator $\gamma A^4 + 1$ doesn't divide the numerator evenly. The GT has a non-trivial rational structure.

**Can a polynomial approximate but not exactly equal the GT?** Let me do a Taylor expansion around A=0:
$$\frac{\beta A^2}{\gamma A^4 + 1} = \beta A^2(1 - \gamma A^4 + \gamma^2 A^8 - ...) = \beta A^2 - \beta\gamma A^6 + ...$$

So $f(A) \approx (\beta - \alpha)A^2 - \beta\gamma A^6 + ...$

This means the GT involves all even powers of A (A^2, A^6, A^10, ...) ŌĆö it's NOT a finite polynomial.

**Therefore, any candidate that is purely a polynomial in A (with finitely many terms) CANNOT match the GT.**
